<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Limit (mathematics)</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Value approached by a mathematical object</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the general concept of limit. For more specific cases, see <a href="/wiki/Limit_of_a_sequence" title="Limit of a sequence">Limit of a sequence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Limit_of_a_function" title="Limit of a function">Limit of a function</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Limit_(disambiguation)#Mathematics" title="Limit (disambiguation)">Limit § Mathematics</a>.</div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, a <b>limit</b> is the value that a <a href="/wiki/Function_(mathematics)" title="Function (mathematics)">function</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Sequence" title="Sequence">sequence</a>) approaches as the input (or index) approaches some <a href="/wiki/Value_(mathematics)" title="Value (mathematics)">value</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Limits are essential to <a href="/wiki/Calculus" title="Calculus">calculus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_analysis" title="Mathematical analysis">mathematical analysis</a>, and are used to define <a href="/wiki/Continuous_function" title="Continuous function">continuity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derivative" title="Derivative">derivatives</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Integral" title="Integral">integrals</a>.
</p><p>The concept of a <a href="/wiki/Limit_of_a_sequence" title="Limit of a sequence">limit of a sequence</a> is further generalized to the concept of a limit of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Net_(topology)" title="Net (topology)">topological net</a>, and is closely related to <a href="/wiki/Limit_(category_theory)" title="Limit (category theory)">limit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Direct_limit" title="Direct limit">direct limit</a> in <a href="/wiki/Category_theory" title="Category theory">category theory</a>.
</p><p>In formulas, a limit of a function is usually written as
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \lim _{x\to c}f(x)=L,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<munder>
<mo form="prefix" movablelimits="true">lim</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">→<!-- → --></mo>
<mi>c</mi>
</mrow>
</munder>
<mi>f</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>L</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lim _{x\to c}f(x)=L,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \lim _{x\to c}f(x)=L,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f5c4adc667e687e332a498508b01cda56fbfc208" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:13.428ex; height:3.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>(although a few authors may use "Lt" instead of "lim"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup>)
and is read as "the limit of <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i></span> of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> as <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> approaches <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">c</span> equals <span class="texhtml"><i>L</i></span>". The fact that a function <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i></span> approaches the limit <span class="texhtml"><i>L</i></span> as <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> approaches <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">c</span> is sometimes denoted by a right arrow (→ or <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \rightarrow }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo stretchy="false">→<!-- → --></mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \rightarrow }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\rightarrow " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/53e574cc3aa5b4bf5f3f5906caf121a378eef08b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.324ex; height:1.843ex;"/></span>), as in
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(x)\to L{\text{ as }}x\to c,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext> as </mtext>

<mi>c</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f(x)\to L{\text{ as }}x\to c,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle f(x)\to L{\text{ as }}x\to c,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9575becabc5842c03bcc138566dc6b395d2a9db" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:19.452ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>which reads "<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/132e57acb643253e7810ee9702d9581f159a1c61" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.279ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> tends to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle L}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mi>L</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle L}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="L" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/103168b86f781fe6e9a4a87b8ea1cebe0ad4ede8" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.583ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> as <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</semantics>

</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%A9goire_de_Saint-Vincent" title="Grégoire de Saint-Vincent">Grégoire de Saint-Vincent</a> gave the first definition of limit (terminus) of a <a href="/wiki/Geometric_series" title="Geometric series">geometric series</a> in his work <i>Opus Geometricum</i> (1647): "The <i>terminus</i> of a progression is the end of the series, which none progression can reach, even not if she is continued in infinity, but which she can approach nearer than a given segment."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>The modern definition of a limit goes back to <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Bolzano" title="Bernard Bolzano">Bernard Bolzano</a> who, in 1817, introduced the basics of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epsilon-delta" title="Epsilon-delta">epsilon-delta</a> technique to define continuous functions. However, his work was not known during his lifetime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Augustin-Louis_Cauchy" title="Augustin-Louis Cauchy">Augustin-Louis Cauchy</a> in 1821,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Larson_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Larson-5">[5]</a></sup> followed by <a href="/wiki/Karl_Weierstrass" title="Karl Weierstrass">Karl Weierstrass</a>, formalized the definition of the limit of a function which became known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/(%CE%B5,_%CE%B4)-definition_of_limit" title="(ε, δ)-definition of limit">(ε, δ)-definition of limit</a>.
</p><p>The modern notation of placing the arrow below the limit symbol is due to <a href="/wiki/G._H._Hardy" title="G. H. Hardy">G. H. Hardy</a>, who introduced it in his book <i><a href="/wiki/A_Course_of_Pure_Mathematics" title="A Course of Pure Mathematics">A Course of Pure Mathematics</a></i> in 1908.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types_of_limits">Types of limits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Types of limits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_sequences">In sequences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: In sequences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Real_numbers">Real numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Real numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Limit_of_a_sequence" title="Limit of a sequence">Limit of a sequence</a></div>
<p>The expression <a href="/wiki/0.999..." title="0.999...">0.999...</a> should be interpreted as the limit of the sequence 0.9, 0.99, 0.999, ... and so on. This sequence can be rigorously shown to have the limit 1, and therefore this expression is meaningfully interpreted as having the value 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>Formally, suppose <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i><sub>1</sub>, <i>a</i><sub>2</sub>, …</span> is a <a href="/wiki/Sequence" title="Sequence">sequence</a> of <a href="/wiki/Real_number" title="Real number">real numbers</a>. When the limit of the sequence exists, the real number <span class="texhtml"><i>L</i></span> is the <i>limit</i> of this sequence if and only if for every <a href="/wiki/Real_number" title="Real number">real number</a> <span class="texhtml"><i>ε</i> &gt; 0</span>, there exists a <a href="/wiki/Natural_number" title="Natural number">natural number</a> <span class="texhtml"><i>N</i></span> such that for all <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> &gt; <i>N</i></span>, we have <span class="texhtml">|<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em;"><i>a</i><sub><i>n</i></sub> − <i>L</i></span>| &lt; <i>ε</i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>
The notation
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \lim _{n\to \infty }a_{n}=L}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<munder>
<mo form="prefix" movablelimits="true">lim</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">→<!-- → --></mo>
<mi mathvariant="normal">∞<!-- ∞ --></mi>
</mrow>
</munder>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>L</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lim _{n\to \infty }a_{n}=L}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle \lim _{n\to \infty }a_{n}=L}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ec8a6da951ff8db5ca56f8e9454ed61271cf6ffd" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:11.789ex; height:3.676ex;"/></div>
is often used, and which is read as
</p>
<dl><dd>"The limit of <i>a<sub>n</sub></i> as <i>n</i> approaches infinity equals <i>L</i>"</dd></dl>
<p>The formal definition intuitively means that eventually, all elements of the sequence get arbitrarily close to the limit, since the <a href="/wiki/Absolute_value" title="Absolute value">absolute value</a> <span class="texhtml">|<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em;"><i>a</i><sub><i>n</i></sub> − <i>L</i></span>|</span> is the distance between <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i><sub><i>n</i></sub></span> and <span class="texhtml"><i>L</i></span>. 
</p><p>Not every sequence has a limit. If it does, then it is called <i><a href="/wiki/Convergent_series" title="Convergent series">convergent</a></i>, and if it does not, then it is <i>divergent</i>. One can show that a convergent sequence has only one limit.
</p><p>The limit of a sequence and the limit of a function are closely related. On one hand, the limit as <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> approaches infinity of a sequence <span class="texhtml">{<i>a</i><sub><i>n</i></sub>}</span> is simply the limit at infinity of a function <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i>(<i>n</i>)</span>—defined on the <a href="/wiki/Natural_number" title="Natural number">natural numbers</a> <span class="texhtml">{<i>n</i>}</span>. On the other hand, if <span class="texhtml"><i>X</i></span> is the domain of a function <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>)</span> and if the limit as <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> approaches infinity of <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i><sub><i>n</i></sub>)</span> is <span class="texhtml"><i>L</i></span> for <i>every</i> arbitrary sequence of points <span class="texhtml">{<i>x</i><sub><i>n</i></sub>}</span> in <span class="texhtml">{<i>X</i> – {<i>x</i><sub>0</sub>}}</span> which converges to <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sub>0</sub></span>, then the limit of the function <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>)</span> as <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i></span> approaches <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sub>0</sub></span> is <span class="texhtml"><i>L</i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> One such sequence would be <span class="texhtml">{<i>x</i><sub>0</sub> + 1/<i>n</i>}</span>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Infinity_as_a_limit">Infinity as a limit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Infinity as a limit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>There is also a notion of having a limit "at infinity", as opposed to at some finite <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle L}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mstyle>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="L" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/103168b86f781fe6e9a4a87b8ea1cebe0ad4ede8" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.583ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>. A sequence <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<msub>
<mi>a</mi>

</mrow>

</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\{a_{n}\}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/339d461b497fb8f8670bb29308fe09f0e7bfd34a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.773ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> is said to "tend to infinity" if, for each real number <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle M&gt;0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<semantics>

<mi>n</mi>
<mo>&gt;</mo>
<mi>N</mi>

That is, for every possible bound, the magnitude of the sequence eventually exceeds the bound. This is often written <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \lim _{n\rightarrow \infty }a_{n}=\infty }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

Such sequences are also called unbounded.
</p><p>It is possible for a sequence to be divergent, but not tend to infinity. Such sequences are called <b>oscillatory</b>. An example of an oscillatory sequence is <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a_{n}=(-1)^{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mrow>
</msub>

<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<msup>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>

</p><p>For the real numbers, there are corresponding notions of tending to positive infinity and negative infinity, by removing the modulus sign from the above definition:
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a_{n}&gt;M.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

defines tending to positive infinity, while 
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle -a_{n}&gt;M.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

defines tending to negative infinity.
</p><p>Sequences which do not tend to infinity are called bounded. Sequences which do not tend to positive infinity are called bounded above, while those which do not tend to negative infinity are bounded below.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Metric_space">Metric space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Metric space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The discussion of sequences above is for sequences of real numbers. The notion of limits can be defined for sequences valued in more abstract spaces. One example of a more abstract space is <a href="/wiki/Metric_space" title="Metric space">metric spaces</a>. If <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle M}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</semantics>

<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>M</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle M}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="M" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f82cade9898ced02fdd08712e5f0c0151758a0dd" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.442ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, then the limit (when it exists) of the sequence is an element <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a\in M}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</semantics>

is satisfied.
</p><p>An equivalent statement is that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a_{n}\rightarrow a}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Topological_space">Topological space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Topological space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In some sense the <i>most</i> abstract space in which limits can be defined are <a href="/wiki/Topological_space" title="Topological space">topological spaces</a>. If <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle X}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mstyle>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X}</annotation>

</math></span><img alt="X" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is a topological space with topology <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \tau }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Function_space">Function space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Function space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>This section deals with the idea of limits of sequences of functions, not to be confused with the idea of limits of functions, discussed below.
</p><p>The field of <a href="/wiki/Functional_analysis" title="Functional analysis">functional analysis</a> partly seeks to identify useful notions of convergence on function spaces. For example, consider the space of functions from a generic set <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle E}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>E</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle E}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="E" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4232c9de2ee3eec0a9c0a19b15ab92daa6223f9b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.776ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {R} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/786849c765da7a84dbc3cce43e96aad58a5868dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>. Given a sequence of functions <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{f_{n}\}_{n&gt;0}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>Then the sequence <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f_{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/132e57acb643253e7810ee9702d9581f159a1c61" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.279ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>. However, such sequences can exhibit unexpected behavior. For example, it is possible to construct a sequence of continuous functions which has a discontinuous pointwise limit. 
</p><p>Another notion of convergence is <a href="/wiki/Uniform_convergence" title="Uniform convergence">uniform convergence</a>. The uniform distance between two functions <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f,g:E\rightarrow \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f,g:E\rightarrow \mathbb {R} }</annotation>

</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle f,g:E\rightarrow \mathbb {R} }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0c22ad0213274b238cc7508121b2f7fdb3f7cd31" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:12.433ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> is the maximum difference between the two functions as the argument <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x\in E}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle d(f,g)=\max _{x\in E}|f(x)-g(x)|.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

Then the sequence <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f_{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

</msub>

<mi>f</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f_{n}\rightarrow f}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle f_{n}\rightarrow f}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b75254f8ef8def12911668e5a259683d1bc92489" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:7.25ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> with respect to this distance. The uniform limit has "nicer" properties than the pointwise limit. For example, the uniform limit of a sequence of continuous functions is continuous.
</p><p>Many different notions of convergence can be defined on function spaces. This is sometimes dependent on the <a href="/wiki/Smoothness" title="Smoothness"> regularity</a> of the space. Prominent examples of function spaces with some notion of convergence are <a href="/wiki/Lp_space" title="Lp space">Lp spaces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sobolev_space" title="Sobolev space">Sobolev space</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_functions">In functions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: In functions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Limit_of_a_function" title="Limit of a function">Limit of a function</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Limit-at-infinity-graph.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="405" data-file-width="619" decoding="async" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Limit-at-infinity-graph.png/300px-Limit-at-infinity-graph.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Limit-at-infinity-graph.png/450px-Limit-at-infinity-graph.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Limit-at-infinity-graph.png/600px-Limit-at-infinity-graph.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Limit-at-infinity-graph.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A function <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>)</span> for which the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Limit_at_infinity" title="Limit at infinity">limit at infinity</a> is <span class="texhtml"><i>L</i></span>. For any arbitrary distance <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ε</span>, there must be a value <span class="texhtml"><i>S</i></span> such that the function stays within <span class="texhtml"><i>L</i> ± <i>ε</i></span> for all <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i> &gt; <i>S</i></span>.</div></div></div><p>Suppose <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i></span> is a <a href="/wiki/Real-valued_function" title="Real-valued function">real-valued function</a> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">c</span> is a <a href="/wiki/Real_number" title="Real number">real number</a>. Intuitively speaking, the expression
</p><dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \lim _{x\to c}f(x)=L}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<munder>
<mo form="prefix" movablelimits="true">lim</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">→<!-- → --></mo>
<mi>c</mi>
</mrow>
</munder>
<mi>f</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>L</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lim _{x\to c}f(x)=L}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\lim _{x\to c}f(x)=L" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c3f174c16cc9e61932ecc7eb71b27a4f10a44fc9" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:12.781ex; height:3.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>means that <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>)</span> can be made to be as close to <span class="texhtml"><i>L</i></span> as desired, by making <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> sufficiently close to <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">c</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>  In that case, the above equation can be read as "the limit of <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i></span> of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span>, as <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> approaches <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">c</span>, is <span class="texhtml"><i>L</i></span>".
</p><p>Formally, the definition of the "limit of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(x)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f(x)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f(x)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/202945cce41ecebb6f643f31d119c514bec7a074" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.418ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> as <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mstyle>

</semantics>

<semantics>

</mstyle>

</semantics>

The limit is a real number <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle L}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

This is known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/(%CE%B5,_%CE%B4)-definition_of_limit" title="(ε, δ)-definition of limit">(ε, δ)-definition of limit</a>. 
</p><p>The inequality <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle 0&lt;|x-c|}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>It can be proven that there is an equivalent definition which makes manifest the connection between limits of sequences and limits of functions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dexter_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-dexter-11">[11]</a></sup> The equivalent definition is given as follows. </mrow>

</semantics>

</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \{f(x_{n})\}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b812683a8c13e52f6fa37645f569e91cfab060bb" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:7.961ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>, the image of the sequence under <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

The limit is a real number <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle L}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="One-sided_limit">One-sided limit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: One-sided limit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/One-sided_limit" title="One-sided limit">one-sided limit</a></div>
<p>It is possible to define the notion of having a limit "from above" or "left limit", and a notion of a limit "from below" or "right limit". These need not agree. An example is given by the positive <a href="/wiki/Indicator_function" title="Indicator function">indicator function</a>, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f:\mathbb {R} \rightarrow \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
<mo>:</mo>

</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Infinity_in_limits_of_functions">Infinity in limits of functions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Infinity in limits of functions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>It is possible to define the notion of "tending to infinity" in the domain of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mstyle>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f}</annotation>
</semantics>

<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \lim _{x\rightarrow \infty }f(x)=L.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

</p><p>In this expression, the infinity is considered to be signed: either <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle +\infty }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

The "limit of f as x tends to positive infinity" is defined as follows. It is a real number <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle L}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mo>&gt;</mo>

</mstyle>

Equivalently, for any sequence <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x_{n}\rightarrow +\infty }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>It is also possible to define the notion of "tending to infinity" in the value of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \lim _{x\rightarrow c}f(x)=\infty .}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>The definition is given as follows. Given any real number <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle M&gt;0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

Equivalently, for any sequence <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x_{n}\rightarrow c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nonstandard_analysis">Nonstandard analysis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Nonstandard analysis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-standard_analysis" title="Non-standard analysis">non-standard analysis</a> (which involves a <a href="/wiki/Hyperreal_number" title="Hyperreal number">hyperreal</a> enlargement of the number system), the limit of a sequence <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle (a_{n})}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (a_{n})}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="(a_{n})" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/18bc33c7c35d82b00f88d3a9103ed4738cde41f9" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.258ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> can be expressed as the <a href="/wiki/Standard_part_function" title="Standard part function">standard part</a> of the value <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a_{H}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>H</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a_{H}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="a_{H}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f55df42c38bfeb8723ab2e49bd5b1bcf72592f57" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.921ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> of the natural extension of the sequence at an infinite <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hypernatural" title="Hypernatural">hypernatural</a> index <i>n=H</i>.  Thus,
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \lim _{n\to \infty }a_{n}=\operatorname {st} (a_{H}).}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<munder>
<mo form="prefix" movablelimits="true">lim</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">→<!-- → --></mo>
<mi mathvariant="normal">∞<!-- ∞ --></mi>
</mrow>
</munder>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>st</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>H</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lim _{n\to \infty }a_{n}=\operatorname {st} (a_{H}).}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \lim _{n\to \infty }a_{n}=\operatorname {st} (a_{H}).}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4676ea014764a9b73a1090d50b4311483fe761b4" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:17.405ex; height:3.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Here, the standard part function "st" rounds off each finite hyperreal number to the nearest real number (the difference between them is <a href="/wiki/Infinitesimal" title="Infinitesimal">infinitesimal</a>). This formalizes the natural intuition that for "very large" values of the index, the terms in the sequence are "very close" to the limit value of the sequence. Conversely, the standard part of a hyperreal <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a=[a_{n}]}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>a</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo stretchy="false">[</mo>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo stretchy="false">]</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a=[a_{n}]}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="a=[a_{n}]" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a9e2180fadc958d8270f9131db9238ff0c1f5392" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:8.07ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> represented in the ultrapower construction by a Cauchy sequence <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle (a_{n})}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (a_{n})}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="(a_{n})" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/18bc33c7c35d82b00f88d3a9103ed4738cde41f9" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.258ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>, is simply the limit of that sequence:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \operatorname {st} (a)=\lim _{n\to \infty }a_{n}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>a</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<munder>
<mo form="prefix" movablelimits="true">lim</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">→<!-- → --></mo>
<mi mathvariant="normal">∞<!-- ∞ --></mi>
</mrow>
</munder>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \operatorname {st} (a)=\lim _{n\to \infty }a_{n}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \operatorname {st} (a)=\lim _{n\to \infty }a_{n}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8f5f102bda6b786a26255699785cbae4f7bfd865" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:15.713ex; height:3.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>In this sense, taking the limit and taking the standard part are equivalent procedures.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Limit_sets">Limit sets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Limit sets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Limit_set_of_a_sequence">Limit set of a sequence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Limit set of a sequence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Let <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}_{n&gt;0}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mi>n</mi>

</msub>

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>&gt;</mo>
<mn>0</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}_{n&gt;0}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}_{n&gt;0}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4117716445d848f807c3c22d7ffb148aede40b8d" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:8.092ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> be a sequence in a topological space <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle X}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="X" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>. For concreteness, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle X}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>X</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="X" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> can be thought of as <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {R} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/786849c765da7a84dbc3cce43e96aad58a5868dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, but the definitions hold more generally. The <a href="/wiki/Limit_set" title="Limit set">limit set</a> is the set of points such that if there is a convergent <a href="/wiki/Subsequence" title="Subsequence">subsequence</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{a_{n_{k}}\}_{k&gt;0}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msub>
<mi>n</mi>

<mi>k</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msub>

<mn>0</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \{a_{n_{k}}\}_{k&gt;0}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \{a_{n_{k}}\}_{k&gt;0}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5c3f19301d4ec197e1ccf41b34fb3b43300f0a5f" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:8.822ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> with <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a_{n_{k}}\rightarrow a}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="a" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ffd2487510aa438433a2579450ab2b3d557e5edc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.23ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> belongs to the limit set. In this context, such an <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>a</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="a" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ffd2487510aa438433a2579450ab2b3d557e5edc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.23ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> is sometimes called a limit point.
</p><p>A use of this notion is to characterize the "long-term behavior" of oscillatory sequences. For example, consider the sequence <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a_{n}=(-1)^{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>

Starting from n=1, the first few terms of this sequence are <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle -1,+1,-1,+1,\cdots }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

It can be checked that it is oscillatory, so has no limit, but has limit points <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{-1,+1\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Limit_set_of_a_trajectory">Limit set of a trajectory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Limit set of a trajectory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>This notion is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dynamical_systems" title="Dynamical systems">dynamical systems</a>, to study limits of trajectories. Defining a trajectory to be a function <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \gamma :\mathbb {R} \rightarrow X}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>γ<!-- γ --></mi>
<mo>:</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
<mo stretchy="false">→<!-- → --></mo>
<mi>X</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \gamma :\mathbb {R} \rightarrow X}</annotation>
</semantics>

The limit set of a trajectory is defined as follows. To any sequence of increasing times <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{t_{n}\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

If <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>Technically, this is the <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \omega }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

The corresponding limit set for sequences of decreasing time is called the <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \alpha }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>An illustrative example is the circle trajectory: <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \gamma (t)=(\cos(t),\sin(t))}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Uses">Uses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Uses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Limits are used to define a number of important concepts in analysis.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Series">Series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Series_(mathematics)" title="Series (mathematics)">series (mathematics)</a></div>
<p>A particular expression of interest which is formalized as the limit of a sequence is sums of infinite series. These are "infinite sums" of real numbers, generally written as
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \sum _{n=1}^{\infty }a_{n}.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<munderover>
<mo>∑<!-- ∑ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">∞<!-- ∞ --></mi>
</mrow>
</munderover>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \sum _{n=1}^{\infty }a_{n}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle \sum _{n=1}^{\infty }a_{n}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/093324aa67e326b9c278246cef10a203e9c5f9ce" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:6.837ex; height:6.843ex;"/></div>
This is defined through limits as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dexter_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-dexter-11">[11]</a></sup> given a sequence of real numbers <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">{</mo>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">}</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\{a_{n}\}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/339d461b497fb8f8670bb29308fe09f0e7bfd34a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.773ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>, the sequence of partial sums is defined by
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle s_{n}=\sum _{i=1}^{n}a_{i}.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>s</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<munderover>
<mo>∑<!-- ∑ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</munderover>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle s_{n}=\sum _{i=1}^{n}a_{i}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle s_{n}=\sum _{i=1}^{n}a_{i}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a15b8f8d0da982e4383b3c100de66307169c1e44" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:11.826ex; height:6.843ex;"/></div>
If the limit of the sequence <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{s_{n}\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">{</mo>

<mi>s</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>

</mstyle>
</mrow>

</semantics>

<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">∞<!-- ∞ --></mi>
</mrow>
</munderover>

<mi>a</mi>

<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \sum _{n=1}^{\infty }a_{n}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \sum _{n=1}^{\infty }a_{n}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fbf33b91e1eb05d0530e73e355823f3c07821381" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:6.19ex; height:6.843ex;"/></span> is defined to be the limit. Otherwise, the series is said to be divergent.
</p><p>A classic example is the <a href="/wiki/Basel_problem" title="Basel problem">Basel problem</a>, where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a_{n}=1/n^{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>/</mo>
</mrow>
<msup>
<mi>n</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a_{n}=1/n^{2}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle a_{n}=1/n^{2}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fdf356d18df7f52a0bc7f6fee82831d2987aca72" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:10.321ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span>. Then 
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \sum _{n=1}^{\infty }{\frac {1}{n^{2}}}={\frac {\pi ^{2}}{6}}.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<munderover>
<mo>∑<!-- ∑ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">∞<!-- ∞ --></mi>
</mrow>
</munderover>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mn>1</mn>
<msup>
<mi>n</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<msup>
<mi>π<!-- π --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mn>6</mn>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \sum _{n=1}^{\infty }{\frac {1}{n^{2}}}={\frac {\pi ^{2}}{6}}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle \sum _{n=1}^{\infty }{\frac {1}{n^{2}}}={\frac {\pi ^{2}}{6}}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/664617be29449b83fe4c47625907f1713ec4b523" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:13.997ex; height:6.843ex;"/></div>
</p><p>However, while for sequences there is essentially a unique notion of convergence, for series there are different notions of convergence. This is due to the fact that the expression <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \sum _{n=1}^{\infty }a_{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<munderover>
<mo>∑<!-- ∑ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">∞<!-- ∞ --></mi>
</mrow>
</munderover>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \sum _{n=1}^{\infty }a_{n}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \sum _{n=1}^{\infty }a_{n}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fbf33b91e1eb05d0530e73e355823f3c07821381" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:6.19ex; height:6.843ex;"/></span> does not discriminate between different orderings of the sequence <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">{</mo>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">}</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\{a_{n}\}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/339d461b497fb8f8670bb29308fe09f0e7bfd34a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.773ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>, while the convergence properties of the sequence of partial sums <i>can</i> depend on the ordering of the sequence. 
</p><p>A series which converges for all orderings is called <b>unconditionally convergent</b>. It can be proven to be equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Absolute_convergence" title="Absolute convergence">absolute convergence</a>. This is defined as follows. A series is absolutely convergent if <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \sum _{n=1}^{\infty }|a_{n}|}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<munderover>
<mo>∑<!-- ∑ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">∞<!-- ∞ --></mi>
</mrow>
</munderover>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \sum _{n=1}^{\infty }|a_{n}|}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \sum _{n=1}^{\infty }|a_{n}|}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/12fdffb4f3f1cf10fadf3723f031f22a37336b71" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:7.484ex; height:6.843ex;"/></span> is well defined. Furthermore, all possible orderings give the same value.
</p><p>Otherwise, the series is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conditionally_convergent" title="Conditionally convergent">conditionally convergent</a>. A surprising result for conditionally convergent series is the <a href="/wiki/Riemann_series_theorem" title="Riemann series theorem">Riemann series theorem</a>: depending on the ordering, the partial sums can be made to converge to any real number, as well as <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \pm \infty }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo>±<!-- ± --></mo>
<mi mathvariant="normal">∞<!-- ∞ --></mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \pm \infty }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\pm \infty " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c586ae37f8efec026b8a4ea3f6a5253576c2c4e6" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:4.132ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Power_series">Power series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Power series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Power_series" title="Power series">power series</a></div>
<p>A useful application of the theory of sums of series is for power series. These are sums of series of the form
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(z)=\sum _{n=0}^{\infty }c_{n}z^{n}.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>z</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<munderover>
<mo>∑<!-- ∑ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>0</mn>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">∞<!-- ∞ --></mi>
</mrow>
</munderover>
<msub>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msup>
<mi>z</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f(z)=\sum _{n=0}^{\infty }c_{n}z^{n}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle f(z)=\sum _{n=0}^{\infty }c_{n}z^{n}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f09d6e64a88abe2e5b6b817baf8a2883c28a33c3" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:16.198ex; height:6.843ex;"/></div>
Often <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle z}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>z</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle z}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="z" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bf368e72c009decd9b6686ee84a375632e11de98" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.088ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> is thought of as a complex number, and a suitable notion of convergence of complex sequences is needed. The set of values of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle z\in \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>z</mi>
<mo>∈<!-- ∈ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle z\in \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle z\in \mathbb {C} }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/169fae60c23a2027ece2aa7fd4b5047492887e91" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:5.607ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> for which the series sum converges is a circle, with its radius known as the <a href="/wiki/Radius_of_convergence" title="Radius of convergence">radius of convergence</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Continuity_of_a_function_at_a_point">Continuity of a function at a point</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Continuity of a function at a point">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The definition of continuity at a point is given through limits.
</p><p>The above definition of a limit is true even if <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(c)\neq L}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>c</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>≠<!-- ≠ --></mo>
<mi>L</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f(c)\neq L}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f(c) \neq L" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/18baf4dce5b2c8d7c02c4e85c022105952910004" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:8.776ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>. Indeed, the function <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i></span> need not even be defined at <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">c</span>. However, if <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(c)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>c</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f(c)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f(c)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/97d4cbf97e497bd1b20228d6a1c12f5f34b87213" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.095ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> is defined and is equal to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle L}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>L</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle L}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="L" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/103168b86f781fe6e9a4a87b8ea1cebe0ad4ede8" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.583ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, then the function is said to be <b>continuous at the point </b><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>c</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="c" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/86a67b81c2de995bd608d5b2df50cd8cd7d92455" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.007ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>.
</p><p>Equivalently, the function is continuous at <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</p><p>An example of a limit where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<semantics>

<mi>c</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="c" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/86a67b81c2de995bd608d5b2df50cd8cd7d92455" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.007ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> is given below.
</p><p>Consider the function
</p><p><div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(x)={\frac {x^{2}-1}{x-1}}.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow>
<msup>

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</mrow>

<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f(x)={\frac {x^{2}-1}{x-1}}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle f(x)={\frac {x^{2}-1}{x-1}}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ef3ab8444df18b621fd612bf7f1edf8f3e3f3844" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:15.386ex; height:5.843ex;"/></div>
</p><p>then <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(1)</span> is not defined (see <a href="/wiki/Indeterminate_form" title="Indeterminate form">Indeterminate form</a>), yet as <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> moves arbitrarily close to 1, <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>)</span> correspondingly approaches 2:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tbody><tr>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(0.9)</span></td>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(0.99)</span></td>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(0.999)</span></td>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(1.0)</span></td>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(1.001)</span></td>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(1.01)</span></td>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(1.1)</span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="texhtml">1.900</span></td>
<td><span class="texhtml">1.990</span></td>
<td><span class="texhtml">1.999</span></td>
<td><span class="texhtml">undefined</span></td>
<td><span class="texhtml">2.001</span></td>
<td><span class="texhtml">2.010</span></td>
<td><span class="texhtml">2.100</span>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Thus, <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>)</span> can be made arbitrarily close to the limit of 2—just by making <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> sufficiently close to <span class="texhtml">1</span>.
</p><p>In other words,
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \lim _{x\to 1}{\frac {x^{2}-1}{x-1}}=2.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \lim _{x\to 1}{\frac {x^{2}-1}{x-1}}=1+1=2.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>In addition to limits at finite values, functions can also have limits at infinity. For example, consider the function
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f(x)={\frac {2x-1}{x}}}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mfrac>
