<mi>x</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
<mi>x</mi>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f(x)={\frac {2x-1}{x}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle f(x)={\frac {2x-1}{x}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fe98ae2a5d981af203c092705320d924a5f10068" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:14.847ex; height:5.176ex;"/></div>
where:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(100) = 1.9900</span></li>
<li><span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(1000) = 1.9990</span></li>
<li><span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(10000) = 1.9999</span></li></ul>
<p>As <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> becomes extremely large, the value of <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>)</span> approaches <span class="texhtml">2</span>, and the value of <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>)</span> can be made as close to <span class="texhtml">2</span> as one could wish—by making <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> sufficiently large. So in this case, the limit of <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>)</span> as <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> approaches infinity is <span class="texhtml">2</span>, or in mathematical notation,<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \lim _{x\to \infty }{\frac {2x-1}{x}}=2.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mo stretchy="false">→<!-- → --></mo>

</mrow>

</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Continuous_functions">Continuous functions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Continuous functions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An important class of functions when considering limits are <a href="/wiki/Continuous_function" title="Continuous function">continuous functions</a>. These are precisely those functions which <i>preserve limits</i>, in the sense that if <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/132e57acb643253e7810ee9702d9581f159a1c61" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.279ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> is a continuous function, then whenever <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a_{n}\rightarrow a}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo stretchy="false">→<!-- → --></mo>
<mi>a</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle a_{n}\rightarrow a}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/95096225df1006c18258be3ef1466f839ba576f0" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:7.292ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> in the domain of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</p><p>In the most general setting of topological spaces, a short proof is given below:
</p><p>Let <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f:X\rightarrow Y}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</semantics>

By definition, for each open set <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle V}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<semantics>

</math></span><img alt="Y" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/961d67d6b454b4df2301ac571808a3538b3a6d3f" style="vertical-align: -0.171ex; width:1.773ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span>, the preimage <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f^{-1}(V)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

This concludes the proof.
</p><p>In real analysis, for the more concrete case of real-valued functions defined on a subset <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle E\subset \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>E</mi>
<mo>⊂<!-- ⊂ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle E\subset \mathbb {R} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle E\subset \mathbb {R} }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6b49e6f675856c92bee1a44a7465a127b2ce06f4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.552ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, that is, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f:E\rightarrow \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
<mo>:</mo>
<mi>E</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">→<!-- → --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f:E\rightarrow \mathbb {R} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f:E\rightarrow \mathbb {R} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/91e6b3cc2fb38e5eb2bbd46c677ff3478275d768" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:10.284ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>, a continuous function may also be defined as a function which is continuous at every point of its domain.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Limit_points">Limit points</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Limit points">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Topology" title="Topology">topology</a>, limits are used to define <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Limit_point" title="Limit point">limit points</a> of a subset of a topological space, which in turn give a useful characterization of <a href="/wiki/Closed_set" title="Closed set">closed sets</a>.
</p><p>In a topological space <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle X}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>X</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="X" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, consider a subset <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle S}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>S</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="S" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4611d85173cd3b508e67077d4a1252c9c05abca2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.499ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>. A point <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

</mstyle>

</semantics>

<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mi>a</mi>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">}</mo>

</semantics>

</p><p>The reason why <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

Take <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle X=\mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

Then <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle 2\in S}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

But <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle 2}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>A closed set, which is defined to be the complement of an open set, is equivalently any set <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle C}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</semantics>

</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Derivative">Derivative</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Derivative">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Derivative" title="Derivative">derivative</a></div>
<p>The derivative is defined formally as a limit. In the scope of <a href="/wiki/Real_analysis" title="Real analysis">real analysis</a>, the derivative is first defined for real functions <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle f}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>f</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="f" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/132e57acb643253e7810ee9702d9581f159a1c61" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.279ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> defined on a subset <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle E\subset \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>E</mi>
<mo>⊂<!-- ⊂ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle E\subset \mathbb {R} }</annotation>
</semantics>

The derivative at <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x\in E}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>∈<!-- ∈ --></mo>
<mi>E</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>

</semantics>

If the limit
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {f(x+h)-f(x)}{h}}}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

as <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle h\rightarrow 0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle h\rightarrow 0}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle h\rightarrow 0}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f93cbaedc1828297b2cf4da6a3e5e733be7e7e7d" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.116ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> exists, then the derivative at <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>

</semantics>

<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {f(y)-f(x)}{y-x}}.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Properties">Properties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Properties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sequences_of_real_numbers">Sequences of real numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sequences of real numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For sequences of real numbers, a number of properties can be proven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dexter_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-dexter-11">[11]</a></sup> Suppose <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<p><div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {1}{a_{n}}}\rightarrow {\frac {1}{a}}.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cauchy_sequences">Cauchy sequences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Cauchy sequences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cauchy_sequence" title="Cauchy sequence">Cauchy sequence</a></div>
<p>A property of convergent sequences of real numbers is that they are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cauchy_sequences" title="Cauchy sequences">Cauchy sequences</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dexter_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-dexter-11">[11]</a></sup> The definition of a Cauchy sequence <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">{</mo>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">}</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\{a_{n}\}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/339d461b497fb8f8670bb29308fe09f0e7bfd34a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.773ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> is that for every real number <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \epsilon &gt;0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>ϵ<!-- ϵ --></mi>
<mo>&gt;</mo>
<mn>0</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \epsilon &gt;0}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\epsilon &gt;0" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/568095ad3924314374a5ab68fae17343661f2a71" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:5.205ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, there is an <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle N}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>N</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle N}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="N" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f5e3890c981ae85503089652feb48b191b57aae3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.064ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> such that whenever <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle m,n&gt;N}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>m</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>&gt;</mo>
<mi>N</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle m,n&gt;N}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="m,n&gt;N" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bfa46859a96c4fc2561c5a9488980723c4673282" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:9.631ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>, 
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle |a_{m}-a_{n}|&lt;\epsilon .}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>m</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mo>&lt;</mo>
<mi>ϵ<!-- ϵ --></mi>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle |a_{m}-a_{n}|&lt;\epsilon .}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle |a_{m}-a_{n}|&lt;\epsilon .}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a09532f49e3796f71e59a4aac7586539503739cd" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:14.177ex; height:2.843ex;"/></div>
</p><p>Informally, for any arbitrarily small error <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \epsilon }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>ϵ<!-- ϵ --></mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \epsilon }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\epsilon " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c3837cad72483d97bcdde49c85d3b7b859fb3fd2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.944ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>, it is possible to find an interval of diameter <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \epsilon }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>ϵ<!-- ϵ --></mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \epsilon }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\epsilon " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c3837cad72483d97bcdde49c85d3b7b859fb3fd2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.944ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> such that eventually the sequence is contained within the interval. 
</p><p>Cauchy sequences are closely related to convergent sequences. In fact, for sequences of real numbers they are equivalent: any Cauchy sequence is convergent. 
</p><p>In general metric spaces, it continues to hold that convergent sequences are also Cauchy. But the converse is not true: not every Cauchy sequence is convergent in a general metric space. A classic counterexample is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rational_numbers" title="Rational numbers">rational numbers</a>, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Q} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Q</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Q} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Q} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c5909f0b54e4718fa24d5fd34d54189d24a66e9a" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.808ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>, with the usual distance. The sequence of decimal approximations to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {2}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msqrt>
<mn>2</mn>
</msqrt>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt {2}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\sqrt {2}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b4afc1e27d418021bf10898eb44a7f5f315735ff" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.098ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span>, truncated at the <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle n}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>n</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle n}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="n" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a601995d55609f2d9f5e233e36fbe9ea26011b3b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.395ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>th decimal place is a Cauchy sequence, but <i>does not converge in</i> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Q} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Q</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Q} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Q} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c5909f0b54e4718fa24d5fd34d54189d24a66e9a" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.808ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>.
</p><p>A metric space in which every Cauchy sequence is also convergent, that is, Cauchy sequences are equivalent to convergent sequences, is known as a <a href="/wiki/Complete_metric_space" title="Complete metric space">complete metric space</a>.
</p><p>One reason Cauchy sequences can be "easier to work with" than convergent sequences is that they are a property of the sequence <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">{</mo>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">}</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\{a_{n}\}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/339d461b497fb8f8670bb29308fe09f0e7bfd34a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.773ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> alone, while convergent sequences require not just the sequence <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">{</mo>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">}</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\{a_{n}\}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/339d461b497fb8f8670bb29308fe09f0e7bfd34a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.773ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> but also the limit of the sequence <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>a</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="a" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ffd2487510aa438433a2579450ab2b3d557e5edc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.23ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Order_of_convergence">Order of convergence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Order of convergence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Beyond whether or not a sequence <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">{</mo>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">}</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\{a_{n}\}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/339d461b497fb8f8670bb29308fe09f0e7bfd34a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.773ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> converges to a limit <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>a</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="a" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ffd2487510aa438433a2579450ab2b3d557e5edc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.23ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>, it is possible to describe how fast a sequence converges to a limit. One way to quantify this is using the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Order_of_convergence" title="Order of convergence">order of convergence</a> of a sequence.
</p><p>A formal definition of order of convergence can be stated as follows. Suppose <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \{a_{n}\}_{n&gt;0}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mrow>
</msub>
<msub>

<mo>&gt;</mo>
<mn>0</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>

<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="a" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ffd2487510aa438433a2579450ab2b3d557e5edc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.23ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>. Furthermore, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a_{n}\neq a}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

If positive constants <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

then <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a_{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>Order of convergence is used for example the field of <a href="/wiki/Numerical_analysis" title="Numerical analysis">numerical analysis</a>, in error analysis.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Computability">Computability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Computability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Limits can be difficult to compute. There exist limit expressions whose <a href="/wiki/Modulus_of_convergence" title="Modulus of convergence">modulus of convergence</a> is <a href="/wiki/Undecidable_problem" title="Undecidable problem">undecidable</a>. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recursion_theory" title="Recursion theory">recursion theory</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Limit_lemma" title="Limit lemma">limit lemma</a> proves that it is possible to encode undecidable problems using limits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are several theorems or tests that indicate whether the limit exists. These are known as <a href="/wiki/Convergence_tests" title="Convergence tests">convergence tests</a>. Examples include the <a href="/wiki/Ratio_test" title="Ratio test">ratio test</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Squeeze_theorem" title="Squeeze theorem">squeeze theorem</a>. However they may not tell how to compute the limit.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Limit_(mathematics)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Asymptotic_analysis" title="Asymptotic analysis">Asymptotic analysis</a>: a method of describing limiting behavior
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Big_O_notation" title="Big O notation">Big O notation</a>: used to describe the limiting behavior of a function when the argument tends towards a particular value or infinity</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Banach_limit" title="Banach limit">Banach limit</a> defined on the Banach space <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \ell ^{\infty }}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>ℓ<!-- ℓ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">∞<!-- ∞ --></mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \ell ^{\infty }}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\ell^\infty" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8348195cf09473662c6f59e6717722a6fc01d0f4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.845ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> that extends the usual limits.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Convergence_of_random_variables" title="Convergence of random variables">Convergence of random variables</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Convergent_matrix" title="Convergent matrix">Convergent matrix</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Limit_(category_theory)" title="Limit (category theory)">Limit in category theory</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Direct_limit" title="Direct limit">Direct limit</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Inverse_limit" title="Inverse limit">Inverse limit</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Limit_of_a_function" title="Limit of a function">Limit of a function</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/One-sided_limit" title="One-sided limit">One-sided limit</a>: either of the two limits of functions of a real variable <i>x</i>, as <i>x</i> approaches a point from above or below</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_limits" title="List of limits">List of limits</a>: list of limits for common functions</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Squeeze_theorem" title="Squeeze theorem">Squeeze theorem</a>: finds a limit of a function via comparison with two other functions</li></ul></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Limit_superior_and_limit_inferior" title="Limit superior and limit inferior">Limit superior and limit inferior</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Modes_of_convergence" title="Modes of convergence">Modes of convergence</a>
<ul><li>An <a href="/wiki/Modes_of_convergence_(annotated_index)" title="Modes of convergence (annotated index)">annotated index</a></li></ul></li></ul>
